  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_873ffd59-ee3a-45e6-9fd5-d0a6b511672e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/392366-so-i-watched-the-tv-series-and-love-it">So, i watched the TV series and love it, so as i did with Buffy and Vampire Academy(kinda related), but i still feel insecure about this book. Is it really good and captivating? Is it boring? Should i read it even thought i disliked Twilight?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_392366'><a id="like_count_community_question_392366" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/392366?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F395922.The_Awakening">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/9579956-nastashia"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1337226166i/9579956._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/9579956-nastashia">Nastashia</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I read the books first a long time ago before I saw the tv series and I personally enjoyed the first two books....it got a bit weird for me somewhere <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I read the books first a long time ago before I saw the tv series and I personally enjoyed the first two books....it got a bit weird for me somewhere near the end of the 3rd or 4th book (The books I had were compilation books each with I believe 2 or 3 books in them .... so I'm guessing it was more like book 6 lol sorry if I'm confusing you lol). When the series came out I was quite disappointed with it because none of the characters descriptions in my opinion matched the descriptions in the book (In the book Bonnie is short a curly redhead .... so I pictured someone that looked more like a teen version of Annie.... not a super pretty black girl with dark hair... so that really threw me for a loop, as well as the Steffan and Damon characters I pictured them looking quite different as well. Also, much of the storyline and events that happen in the book don't show up in the show at all. I would say at least give the first 2 or 3 books a read and see if they are your cup of tea, but don't expect them to be like the show at all because they are two different beasts.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <span id="freeText15440773888572325750" style="display:none">My god!!! What can I say about this book?? IT IS A BAD BOOK!!! It has bad cheesy prose, a snotty annoying (and kind of a bimbo) heroine and the cliched, brooding Byronic vampire hero, needless to say that the moment they lay their eyes upon each other they fall hopelessly in love. Oh yes!! I can't believe I almost forgot!!!!! The mother of all originalities... it also has a love triangle!!!! I think it's safe to say that this book is the poster book for cheesy YA pnr books and since it was written in 1991 it's even safer to say that the others copied L. J. Smith's tropes and not the other way around.<br />But did I enjoyed it? I am ashamed to admit it...but yes I did!!! This book is a guilty pleasure, pure silly escapism and I'm afraid I will be back for more... <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText7493563991259253970" style="display:none">Read Awakening legally and for free <a href="http://browseinside.harperteen.com/index.aspx?isbn13=9780061963865" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> courtesy of the publisher. But please keep adequate amounts of brain bleach on hand.<br />What can I say? I read this on the usually-safe assumption that the book would be better than its adaptation. Differences are usually in the book's favor, but for once this is not the case. The TV series is a dramatically revised and very loose adaptation of the book, and a HUGE IMPROVEMENT. I'd give the TV series 4 stars, but this book is among the most worthless I have ever read.<br />I was shocked to realize just how bad the book is: atrocious dialogue, Elena is arrogant from the start and does not improve on acquaintance (all the characters are pretty shallow, actually), the romance is woefully artificial, and the plot... what a mess. I was hoping Breaking Dawn would last longer as my "most horrible book of all time." I started this book out of curiosity, kept going for the laughs, got depressed, and finished it for integrity's sake so that I can honestly say I have read and evaluated the whole thing. But there is no way I'm reading Book II.</span>

<div id="review_45614732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45614732" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1803617-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230700083p2/1803617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45614732?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/1803617-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45614732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6535724222896490622">Okay, this was MY Twilight before there was Twilgiht. I read this series when I was about thirteen. I was already into vampires in my preppy goth kind of way, and this one made me say SQUEE! This book is from the early 90's, but with the Twilight phenomenon, it's now been reissued, bound with a new cover featuring some blonde model, and is being considered as the basis of a TV series on CW (not sure how I feel about that). I like the original cover better (featured above). I had to bid on ebay f</span>
  <span id="freeText6535724222896490622" style="display:none">Okay, this was MY Twilight before there was Twilgiht. I read this series when I was about thirteen. I was already into vampires in my preppy goth kind of way, and this one made me say SQUEE! This book is from the early 90's, but with the Twilight phenomenon, it's now been reissued, bound with a new cover featuring some blonde model, and is being considered as the basis of a TV series on CW (not sure how I feel about that). I like the original cover better (featured above). I had to bid on ebay for this baby! <br /><br />Some parts of this are cheesy, but the story is this: Hot, slightly bitchy and arrogant girl-next-door catches the eye of TWO vampire brothers who hate each other. Insert drama here. Then, in the later books, throw in witches and werewolves and angry ancient vampires bent on killing everyone. <br /><br />Plus, it's got rockin' 90's fashions, like hot pink dresses and perms. What's not to love? <br /><br />If you liked Twilight, you'll probably like this. Sometimes I wonder if Stephenie Meyer actually stole some ideas from LJ Smith...some parts are similar, but I guess there's only so many original ways to write about the human girl/vampire boy, Romeo and Juliet-ish storyline before things start to overlap in similarity. They're both YA, they're both "scary romance," they both have cheese, and they're both slightly addictive. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6535724222896490622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/563742-margot?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10567940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer215006537337298106">After reading the vampire trilogy by Stephenie Meyer, I thought I would continue my bloodthirsty fiction rampage with this older teenage vampire trilogy. Lo and behold, it's almost the same story! Oh, Stephenie Meyer, now I know how you cranked out those three fat (should have been heavily edited) books in such a short span of time! For shame!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2998210568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2998210568" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana - Diary of Difference" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana - Diary of Difference" href="/user/show/28198445-ivana---diary-of-difference">Ivana - Diary of Difference</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28198445-ivana---diary-of-difference?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28198445-ivana---diary-of-difference?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2998210568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13560447264346428219"><a href='https://diaryofdifference.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> | <a href='https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> | <a href='https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> | <a href='https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> | <a href='https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a> <br/><br/>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2998210568' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Awakening</a> - ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2998210684' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Struggle</a> - Review Coming Soon!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1571089562i/28293866._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>I had The Awakening and the Struggle (the first and second books from the Vampire Diaries series) on my shelf for years.</i>
</b><br/><br/>When I say years, I mean it. It all started when I was in high-school, around 6 years ago, and I was in love with the Vampire Diaries TV Show. When I found out there are books as well, I begged my mum to buy them for me. And once I had them, I never got to read the</span>
  <span id="freeText13560447264346428219" style="display:none"><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> <br><br>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2998210568" rel="nofollow noopener">The Awakening</a> - ★★★★★<br>#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2998210684" rel="nofollow noopener">The Struggle</a> - Review Coming Soon!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1571089562i/28293866._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>I had The Awakening and the Struggle (the first and second books from the Vampire Diaries series) on my shelf for years.</i>
</b><br><br>When I say years, I mean it. It all started when I was in high-school, around 6 years ago, and I was in love with the Vampire Diaries TV Show. When I found out there are books as well, I begged my mum to buy them for me. And once I had them, I never got to read them, because teenage logic...<br><br>I recently noticed the Vampire Diaries books sitting on my shelf, forgotten, and I thought it would be a perfect opportunity to read it in October, because of the whole spooky vibe. So there it is now - even thought the wheel didn't choose it, I did, because it deserved the attention!<br><br>Elena Gilbert is a popular girl in high-school and she always gets what she wants. Boys want to be with her, girls hate her, or want to be her best friends. And when this new boy Stefan comes into town, all mysterious, Elena wants him. But Stefan is hiding a deadly secret that Elena might now be ready for just yet. And her life, as well as the life of everyone living in Fell's Church is in grave danger... Elena finds herself between two brothers - one who came for a new life, and the other, who came for revenge...<br><br>Reading this book, while already knowing what the plot it, I thought I found find it boring. But no. I still enjoyed every single page of it, and I still devoured this book in one day.<br><br>From the first chapter, this book is intense and captures your attention. It is written in third person, but it also contains diary entries that belong to Elena and capture her deepest thoughts that she doesn't dare share with anyone else.<br><br><b>
  <i>I loved Elena!</i>
</b><br><br>Her character is exactly what I was expected and what I have known to love - brave and fierce, and also willing to sacrifice her own happiness and safety for the people she loves the most. <br><br>Elena's friends, Meredith and Bonnie are the friends every girl needs. Funny and caring. A few pages in, and you will get to love them too.<br><br>Stefan - the mysterious new guy in school. The guy that tries to stay away from the girl he really wants because he's a danger to her. A little bit of Twilight vibes, but we can get past that. Because there is one thing that Twilight didn't have, that you can find reading The Vampire Diaries...<br><br><b>
  <i>DAMON</i>
</b><br><br>Even though we only get a glimpse of him in this book, we can feel his presence throughout the whole book. We can feel his connection with Elena, as weird and spooky as it may be. All that danger that he carries with him, we all want to see whether there's anything good in him at all. His story is the most intriguing one, I think. His hunger for revenge makes you really understand both sides of the story and choose a side for yourself.<br><br><b>
  <i>So, are you team Stefan, or team Damon?</i>
</b><br><br>I loved reading this - it was an amazing experience and it reminded me of my high-school days, of those innocent happy memories. My teenage life didn't include vampires, but hey - it was still awesome!<br><br>Pick the Vampire Diaries up if you love Young Adult spooky books, if you loved Twilight and if you love vampire, love and mystery stories in general.<br><br><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13560447264346428219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16052528453689641601">I came to that book by the internet. A lot of people recommended it and I thought it MUST be right. Gosh, did I failed. <br/>It's one of the first book I was eager to give away and I really regret that I bought it. At first the cover of my german version is ugly (yeah I know, don't judge a book by its cover, but it IS ugly)<br/><br/>Second, I am really fed up with all this "ooohw dark handsome mysterious guy" or even better TWO gorgeous brothers.   <span id="freeText16052528453689641601" style="display:none">I came to that book by the internet. A lot of people recommended it and I thought it MUST be right. Gosh, did I failed. <br />It's one of the first book I was eager to give away and I really regret that I bought it. At first the cover of my german version is ugly (yeah I know, don't judge a book by its cover, but it IS ugly)<br /><br />Second, I am really fed up with all this "ooohw dark handsome mysterious guy" or even better TWO gorgeous brothers. I mean do we normal human girls now all have to wait for our Mr. Handsome? What's about true beauty? The beauty of the heart?<br /><br />Then the next point, Elena the school queen. Talking about cliche. Ugh I really don't want to write about that.<br />While her character isn't very complex, so it is the same with her friends and cute little Stefano, the mysterious loverboy. <br />It's just like "oh I saw you and you're like SO gorgeous! I'll love you forever!". There is no developement, it's just given from the author.<br /><br />And that is a pity, because I started to watch the series on TV and I actually liked it better.<br /><br />UPDATE; Series isn't that much better. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3185404452107195489">Picture the scene. It's 1996, I'm 12 years old. I'm at the library down the street, perusing the single shelf that makes up the YA section. I find this little paperback that promises deadly love. Vampire brothers, you say? Unspeakable horror, you say? I take the book home and read it in the course of an afternoon. I AM AWESTRUCK. WHAT IS THIS MAGICAL BOOK??? I've never read anything like it.<br/><br/>Immediately I make my dad take me to the bookstore in the mall so he can buy me the rest of the series. I </span>
  <span id="freeText3185404452107195489" style="display:none">Picture the scene. It's 1996, I'm 12 years old. I'm at the library down the street, perusing the single shelf that makes up the YA section. I find this little paperback that promises deadly love. Vampire brothers, you say? Unspeakable horror, you say? I take the book home and read it in the course of an afternoon. I AM AWESTRUCK. WHAT IS THIS MAGICAL BOOK??? I've never read anything like it.<br><br>Immediately I make my dad take me to the bookstore in the mall so he can buy me the rest of the series. I spent the rest of my life (or the next few months) in various bookstores tracking down all L.J. Smith books.<br><br>And I've been obsessed ever since. And everyone thought I was weird for liking vampires. But I didn't care! I went on one of those early, early fansites where you could be a keeper of something, and I became a keeper of Damon's ring. I joined some email list of L.J. Smith news, where every email ended with <i>Noblesse Oblige</i>. I own multiple copies of this series.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464468406i/19242596.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This may be my favorite series of hers, although I love them all. But this was my gateway drug. I know people don't like Elena because she's selfish and shallow but that doesn't bother me. It's not that I think people should approve of her behavior or anything, but it's rare to see this type of character as a teenage girl. Her behavior wouldn't be out of place for, say, a late twenties/early thirties womanizing rich businessman or something. More power to Elena, I say.<br><br>I literally don't understand how people think this is bad. WHAT??? I get that they might not like it, but <i>bad</i>? It has a good buildup of creepy events, a tragic backstory, high school drama, a creepy atmosphere, a haunted house scene, a mysterious Power, and vampires!!! Elena is determined, Bonnie is adorable, Meredith is snarky, Matt is a nice guy, and Stefan is somehow not as bad as I remembered. This was top-notch YA back in the day! It ends on a cliffhanger, but if you're reading the new two-book edition, you get to jump right into <i>The Struggle</i>!<br><br>Anyway. I love it. I may have blinders on when it comes to this series but no, obviously I don't, it's amazing.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464469915ra/19242689.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Damon, you have no idea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3185404452107195489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3005927719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3005927719" />
    <a title="Faith M ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587515873p2/29390149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3005927719?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M ✨" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m">Faith M ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=3rd-person">3rd-person</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=a-wizard-did-it">a-wizard-did-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=angels-demons">angels-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-gurl">mc-gurl</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3005927719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5320887193697069983">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/88582854-devanshi-agarwal' rel='nofollow noopener'>Devanshi</a>!<br/><br/>Ok. Anyone who knows me knows that I love two things: Peter Pan and vampires (not necessarily together, but can you imagine!!??) So it comes as no surprise that I love The Vampire Diaries television show. I’ve been a big fan since I was about 12 or so and recently decided to rewatch the show in its entirety. This brought on the nostalgia of when I was reading the books, also at the tender age of 12. I didn’t remember a lot about them (I was a particularly skimmy reader b</span>
  <span id="freeText5320887193697069983" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/88582854-devanshi-agarwal" rel="nofollow noopener">Devanshi</a>!<br /><br />Ok. Anyone who knows me knows that I love two things: Peter Pan and vampires (not necessarily together, but can you imagine!!??) So it comes as no surprise that I love The Vampire Diaries television show. I’ve been a big fan since I was about 12 or so and recently decided to rewatch the show in its entirety. This brought on the nostalgia of when I was reading the books, also at the tender age of 12. I didn’t remember a lot about them (I was a particularly skimmy reader back then) so I figured, why not reread the books as I rewatch the show?<br /><br /><blockquote>The moon had not yet risen, and she could just make out the old graveyard and Wickery Bridge beyond it. The old graveyard dated from Civil War days, and many of the headstones bore the names of soldiers. It had a wild look to it; brambles and tall weeds grew on the graves, and ivy vines swarmed over crumbling granite. Elena had never liked it. “It looks different, doesn’t it? In the dark, I mean,” she said unsteadily. She didn’t know how to say what she really meant, that it was not a place for the living.</blockquote><br />First of all, I was surprised by how good the writing is. Idk what I expected exactly, but well-done prose wasn’t it. It really feels like a spooky movie from the 90s and I really appreciated it.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the rest of this wasn’t as good. The plot suffered significantly from iffy pacing. Instalove was a plague throughout. And worst of all, I absolutely hate the characters.<br /><br />Scratch that. I absolutely hate Elena and Stefan, though really only when they’re together. Or when they’re pining after the other. Or when they breathe in each other’s general direction.<br /><br />Confession time: while I love TVD, I don’t love Elena Gilbert. I think she’s really annoying, actually, and kind of a Mary Sue idiot. But book Elena makes her a saint. A paragon of excellency. The best written protagonist of all time.<br /><br />Primarily, this is because book Elena and show Elena aren’t the same person. They’re entirely different in every conceivable way. Different hair, different eyes, different skin tone, different personality and priorities, different past traumas, different siblings, different friends, different aunt. Book Elena is a mean girl who literally vows to make Stefan her boyfriend solely because he snubs her and she’s used to every male on the planet being obsessed with her. It’s the most ridiculous thing in the world. She acts like it’s some big thing when she just needs a reality check. But then Stefan reveals that he loved her the whole time even though they don’t know each other and have never actually held a conversation for longer than 2 seconds. And from there, it’s true love.<br /><br />Every other character is different from their show counterpart too: Stefan is like 600 years old and still hung up on Katherine, Bonnie is a meek redhead, Caroline is a frenemy rival, and some girl named Meredith who isn’t Meredith Fell is the sarcastic best friend. The only character who’s actually the exact same is Matt.<br /><br />This isn’t a problem. I don’t mind that the show changed the source material so much. They actually made better, more well rounded characters than the original, and improved the plot too. But it’s strange that the showrunners felt the need to change everything so much but keep names and the title of the series the same.<br /><br />I’m definitely going to continue my reread and hopefully make it passed where I dropped the series back in the day. If not for the nostalgia, for my undying desire to know what happens differently.<br /><br /><blockquote>Evil will never find peace. It may triumph, but it will never find peace.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5320887193697069983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151322123" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151322123" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151322123?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780340945018" href="/book/show/1216145.The_Awakening">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151322123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14058495621453927613">If the show had not been made, if I had not read a ton of other vampire books, THE AWAKENING might have been OK. Since the show was made and since I have read a ton of YA PNR with vampires as the central figure… I am amazed that I finished it. <br/><br/>First: This book pales in comparison to the show. So from here on out I am not even going to bother with a comparison.<br/><br/>Second: I hate Elena! Flighty, believing herself entitled, and very insensitive to the needs and feelings of those around her (poor Matt!)</span>
  <span id="freeText14058495621453927613" style="display:none">If the show had not been made, if I had not read a ton of other vampire books, THE AWAKENING might have been OK. Since the show was made and since I have read a ton of YA PNR with vampires as the central figure… I am amazed that I finished it. <br /><br />First: This book pales in comparison to the show. So from here on out I am not even going to bother with a comparison.<br /><br />Second: I hate Elena! Flighty, believing herself entitled, and very insensitive to the needs and feelings of those around her (poor Matt!) I really did not like how she seemed to feel herself entitled (i.e. once she had set her sights on Steffan, nothing mattered: Not her boyfriend. Not her friends.) I suppose I should admire her go get him attitude. Sadly, I just could not! The only thing that I agreed with was her assessment of Katherine. Which leads me to the boys, Steffan and Damon. Nothing new to them. Hot, brooding… bla bla bla. I suppose I am being a tad harsh especially considering that these books were first published in 1991(?) So I suppose they’re trailblazers, the first of their kind at the time… I would not know. <br /><br />But I am stubborn because I’m reading the rest. I intend to answer in the affirmative (and with a straight face) that, yes, I did read the books she got me.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14058495621453927613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_7211133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7211133" />
    <a title="Sarah Pierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/455245-sarah-pierce"><img alt="Sarah Pierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553500p2/455245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7211133?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Pierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Pierce" href="/user/show/455245-sarah-pierce">Sarah Pierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7211133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15827783652978301794">These were some of my favorite books as a teenager. They are about a high school student, Elena Gilbert, who is torn between two hot vampire brothers. Melodrama ensues. They are not the most mature books, but they are all about nostalgia for me. Of course, as I get older, I think that a lot of the things Elena does are downright stupid, but I still remember how romantic it all seemed when I was 14.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_171719794" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171719794?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah S." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah S." href="/user/show/4961662-hannah-s">Hannah S.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4961662-hannah-s?shelf=gave-up-on">gave-up-on</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4961662-hannah-s?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171719794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5194075276295867568">I've watched the tv show for quite a while, which I admit definitely colors my reception of the book. But I could not get past the first few chapters. I tried, because I wanted to see how the books differed from the show. I really did try, which is why I made it to the third chapters instead of the just the first. The writing was sub-par and I just could not relate to any of the characters. They seemed like caricatures, all obsessed with popularity and being the "queen bee," and I just couldn't </span>
  <span id="freeText5194075276295867568" style="display:none">I've watched the tv show for quite a while, which I admit definitely colors my reception of the book. But I could not get past the first few chapters. I tried, because I wanted to see how the books differed from the show. I really did try, which is why I made it to the third chapters instead of the just the first. The writing was sub-par and I just could not relate to any of the characters. They seemed like caricatures, all obsessed with popularity and being the "queen bee," and I just couldn't take it. Sure, girls can be catty in real life, but not quite to that extent. The fact that Stefan could read minds also felt like it was just a Twilight knock-off, though if you asked me, I wouldn't be able to tell you which book was published first. Compared to their tv counterparts, every single character seemed meaner or weaker or too detached for me to feel anything for them at all. I know it's unfair to compare the two, since they are in different media and the plots are vastly different, as well (yes, I admit to looking up the plot summaries of the books, since I couldn't stand to read them myself). My curiosity to see what happened in the plot was not enough to keep me going through the bad writing and horrible characterization, and when I did finally read plot summaries, I wasn't impressed by those either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5194075276295867568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_448746439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/448746439" />
    <a title="Merary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6508812-merary"><img alt="Merary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483176424p2/6508812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/448746439?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merary" href="/user/show/6508812-merary">Merary</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">If you liked Twilight . . . </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=boring-bland-main-characters">boring-bland-main-characters</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6508812-merary?shelf=where-s-the-fucking-conflict">where-s-the-fucking-conflict</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer448746439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5918249186690006434">Well, well, well. This is the book that actually started the cliche storm that influenced the <i>Twilight</i> series. Put it in your book history book (Whaa?), my dear readers!<br/><br/>I haven't seen the TV series yet (I will until I finish the entire series. I can't wait for Nina Dobrev, one of my favorite actresses!), but I'm pretty sure it's so much better than this. I don't know, maybe it was the writing that set me off. I wouldn't say it was terrible, it just wasn't . . . good. I will say it once again: Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText5918249186690006434" style="display:none">Well, well, well. This is the book that actually started the cliche storm that influenced the <i>Twilight</i> series. Put it in your book history book (Whaa?), my dear readers!<br /><br />I haven't seen the TV series yet (I will until I finish the entire series. I can't wait for Nina Dobrev, one of my favorite actresses!), but I'm pretty sure it's so much better than this. I don't know, maybe it was the writing that set me off. I wouldn't say it was terrible, it just wasn't . . . good. I will say it once again: Show, don't tell, goddammit!<br /><br />Since I was more familiar with the TV series, I wasn't expecting Elena to be . . . blonde. And with lapis lazuli blue eyes. Because ordinary blue eyes are too mainstream, I guess. And because brown hair is for ugly girls. Didn't you heard that gentlemen prefer blondes, girls? Okay, here's my problem: Elena is a whiny bimbo. There, I said it. Elena isn't the typical ordinary girl. Instead, she is the Queen Bee and really rich. But, wait! Her life isn't perfect. She wants everything to be perfect, because if she doesn't, her life is ruined! Oh, how my heart aches for her suffering. She has a really nice boyfriend, Matt; <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Who is a monster as well. I spoiled myself by accident. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> the best friends in the world; and of course, a frenemy, Caroline, who wants to take her spot as the most popular in school. And she is a superficial bitch who is willing to have what she wants, because she is also a spoiled parasite.<br /><br />Yawn, yawn. Where's the spice?<br /><br />Then, Stefan arrives. And in case you missed, HE IS A VAMPIRE! Elena immediately falls in love with him and is willing to dump her boyfriend so he can have him. <br />Bitch.<br />Stefan realizes that Elena looks like Katherine, his former lover, and the reason he is a vampire. Katherine also had an affair with Stefan's brother, Damon, who is now his worst enemy. He falls in love with her as well but ignores her for some reason. <br />Stuff happens, blah blah blah, after some angst, they finally get together.<br />It doesn't make me happy, though, considering the fact that their relationship is a bunch of garbage. If that isn't codependency, then I don't know what is! Even Elena said that she will die without him, <i>before they even got together.</i> And he apparently stalks her. Great, that's exactly what we needed: Another creepy YA lover. If doesn't matter, though. Wait, what? Why am I saying that? Let's do a little quiz, shall we?<br /><br />QUESTION TIME!!<br />If you discovered that the guy you liked has a piece of clothing of yours (the one you lost on your second day of school) and you've been officially dating since yesterday, what would you do?<br /><br />a) Call the police.<br />b) Think it was the most romantic gesture somebody has ever done to you.<br />c) RUN. AWAY.<br /><br />If you chose either A or C, then you're not Elena Gilbert.<br />Enough. Said.<br /><br />And where is Damon? Honestly, I didn't pay attention to this after Elena and Stefan got together. Nothing interesting happens from there.<br /><br />Oh yes, I forgot! Someone is murdering innocents in the town! Who is responsible for this heinous crime?<br />I don't think I care.<br /><br />The blurb tells you that there's a love triangle. The only love triangle at the moment is the one between the Salvatore brothers and Katherine. Which happened, like, centuries ago. I'm still intrigued about what will happen with Elena and the Salvatore brothers, though. Okay, yes, this book was predictable, cheesy, with bland characters and plot-less, but I still want to know what will happen next. That's my explanation for the rating I gave for this book.<br /><b>EDIT:</b> The rating is now 2 stars after some consideration.<br /><br />One thing, though: The ending was so messy. That's not a cliffhanger, that is just being lazy!<br />UGH.<br /><br />I'm thinking that I made a really big mistake. Oh, well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5918249186690006434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1857647-j-d-stroube?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44522591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1867502522278034832">After reading this book for the fifth or sixth time, I still enjoyed it! It reminds me of Twilight by Stephenie Meyer. <br/><br/>I have about a million positive things to say and only one negative: Elena says "I love you" too quickly. The fact that such a serious statement is made at such an early stage in the book...irritates me. I love you is not something to be taken lightly, and when said too early it makes me think of puppy love, not undying love.<br/><br/>Other than that single annoyance...this book is endear</span>
  <span id="freeText1867502522278034832" style="display:none">After reading this book for the fifth or sixth time, I still enjoyed it! It reminds me of Twilight by Stephenie Meyer. <br /><br />I have about a million positive things to say and only one negative: Elena says "I love you" too quickly. The fact that such a serious statement is made at such an early stage in the book...irritates me. I love you is not something to be taken lightly, and when said too early it makes me think of puppy love, not undying love.<br /><br />Other than that single annoyance...this book is endearing. It was written years before Twilight and I wonder if Stephenie Meyer may have gotten some of her ideas from this series. <br /><br />Elena is somewhat pretentious in the beginning, but blossoms throughout the book. Her obssession turns to devotion, and her conceited demeanor transforms into a singleminded determination to become someone worthy. <br /><br />Stefan plays the part of the wounded soul. He believes that he is no longer worthy of happiness, and instead seeks to blend into society only to find acceptance in Elena. <br /><br />Damon is an captivating character. Even in the first installment of this series, it is difficult to dislike him. He is the embodiment of sexuality and temptation that only becomes more appetizing in the later parts of the series. <br /><br />I fully recommend this book to anyone who has a fondness for love triangles, and the supernatural. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1867502522278034832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer915415721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4516165629608145222"><b>Less of a review and more of me venting, sorry. You've been warned. </b> I was thinking of starting this off by saying <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/395922.The_Awakening__The_Vampire_Diaries___1_' title='The Awakening (The Vampire Diaries, #1) by L.J. Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Awakening</a> reads like fanfiction, but . . . that would be an insult to fanfiction. <br/><br/>I'm pretty sure the only reason I got through <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/395922.The_Awakening__The_Vampire_Diaries___1_' title='The Awakening (The Vampire Diaries, #1) by L.J. Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Awakening</a> was because I came to the conclusion that Elena has narcissistic personality disorder. On the first day back at school, Elena sees Stephan and decides she's going to <i>have him</i>, even <b>"if it killed her. If it killed both of them, she'd have h</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4516165629608145222" style="display:none"><b>Less of a review and more of me venting, sorry. You've been warned. </b> I was thinking of starting this off by saying <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/395922.The_Awakening__The_Vampire_Diaries___1_" title="The Awakening (The Vampire Diaries, #1) by L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Awakening</a> reads like fanfiction, but . . . that would be an insult to fanfiction. <br /><br />I'm pretty sure the only reason I got through <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/395922.The_Awakening__The_Vampire_Diaries___1_" title="The Awakening (The Vampire Diaries, #1) by L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Awakening</a> was because I came to the conclusion that Elena has narcissistic personality disorder. On the first day back at school, Elena sees Stephan and decides she's going to <i>have him</i>, even <b>"if it killed her. If it killed both of them, she'd have him."</b> (30) Okay, that is not healthy. And also, what, does Stefan not have any say in the matter? I guess not. Apparently he's the first guy to not automatically start fawning all over her. <blockquote>
  <i>"He'd walked right by. Without a glance. She couldn't remember how long it had been since a boy had done that. They all looked, at least. Some whistled. Some stopped to talk. Some just stared."</i>
</blockquote>And then later she starts getting teary eyed because she looks at him and he looks away. That is literally all that happens. She turns in her seat and smiles at him and he looks down at his desk. Elena decides this means Stefan thinks he's better than everyone else. Because of course, it's not possible he's actually shy or anything. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think they speak like once sentence to each other, maybe. And then he saves her from a boy who is basically trying to rape and/or murder her and (yet she's more scared of Stefan!) And then her and Stefan kiss and she tells him she loves him. *gag* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />With that being said, I think I can see where the author was going with this. Two vampire brothers fighting over a human girl. The TV show is popular enough; if the book had been done right, it might've been popular too, albeit a little cliche. <s>Probably not as popular though because the show has Ian Somerhalder *drool* And Katherine is actually a badass on the show.</s> But the bad writing and terrible characterization were too hard to overlook. There is a very, very slim chance I'll read the rest of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4516165629608145222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer98581626" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18085340443336665242">Well, I didn't like this book. Not at all. I read half of the book and then got really really bored so I scanned the pages til the end. I was both relieved and disappointed. Disappointed because the book wasn't good. I did not like the characters - especially Elena. And relieved because I was saved from another half a day of pure stupidity.<br/><br/>Elena's obsession with the Stefan was just too annoying plus there were a bunch of stupidly infuriating scenes that were so, well.. infuriating and stupid. Ta</span>
  <span id="freeText18085340443336665242" style="display:none">Well, I didn't like this book. Not at all. I read half of the book and then got really really bored so I scanned the pages til the end. I was both relieved and disappointed. Disappointed because the book wasn't good. I did not like the characters - especially Elena. And relieved because I was saved from another half a day of pure stupidity.<br /><br />Elena's obsession with the Stefan was just too annoying plus there were a bunch of stupidly infuriating scenes that were so, well.. infuriating and stupid. Take the ribbon she left on the cemetery for example. Because she found out that Stefan has been keeping it, she just stupidly jumped into the conclusion that 'he has always loved me,' 'oh my god!' and then she cried her butt off. I was like: What the hell was that? O.O<br /><br />Poor Elena. She is too obsessed with Stefan that her obsession is eating half of her brain away =.= it didn't even cross her mind that maybe he found it on the cemetery later that time she left it and then decided to keep it.<br /><br />Oh well... I have no intention of actually reading this book til the end nor am I anticipating to read the succeeding books. I might as well start reading other books that actually make sense.</span>

<div id="review_2358747667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358747667" />
    <a title="Kim M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2389794-kim-m"><img alt="Kim M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525186067p2/2389794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2358747667?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim M" href="/user/show/2389794-kim-m">Kim M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=the-movie-was-better">the-movie-was-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=read-it-and-seen-it">read-it-and-seen-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358747667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14960832717362530224"><i>“Since when had she, Elena Gilbert, been scared of meeting people? Since when had she been scared of anything? She stood up and angrily thrust her arms into a red silk kimono. She didn’t even glance at the elaborate Victorian mirror above the cherry wood dresser. She knew what she’d see. Elena Gilbert, cool and blonde and slender, the fashion trendsetter, the high school senior, the girl every boy wanted and every girl wanted to be.”</i><br/><br/>Ladies and gentlemen, introducing…<br/><br/><b>Queen Snowflake!!!!</b><br/><br/>Elena owns</span>
  <span id="freeText14960832717362530224" style="display:none"><i>“Since when had she, Elena Gilbert, been scared of meeting people? Since when had she been scared of anything? She stood up and angrily thrust her arms into a red silk kimono. She didn’t even glance at the elaborate Victorian mirror above the cherry wood dresser. She knew what she’d see. Elena Gilbert, cool and blonde and slender, the fashion trendsetter, the high school senior, the girl every boy wanted and every girl wanted to be.”</i><br /><br />Ladies and gentlemen, introducing…<br /><br /><b>Queen Snowflake!!!!</b><br /><br />Elena owns the school. Everyone adores her, and she’s always surrounded by all her “cool” friends, as well as <i>“four or five hangers-on who hoped to gain popularity by association.”</i> Anything that Elena wants, she gets. But when, on Elena’s first day back to school, the mysterious and exceedingly attractive new student walks straight past her without even looking her way, Elena’s world comes crashing down in shock and horror:<br /><br /><i>"He’d walked right by—without a glance! She couldn’t remember how long it had been since a boy had done that. They all looked, at least. Some whistled, some stopped to talk, some just stared, and that had always been fine with Elena. After all, what was more important than boys? They were the mark of how popular you were, how beautiful you were, and they could be useful for all sorts of things."</i><br /><br />And now, dun dun DUN! New boy didn’t give her the time of day. Poor, poor Elena.<br /><br /><i>The Awakening</i> is the story of an exceedingly privileged high school girl who falls insta-in-love with the new kid in town, who just so happens to be a 500-year-old vampire. When she thinks he somehow didn’t fall insta-in-love back (don’t worry, he really did, she just doesn’t know it), she sees it as a great challenge and begins using her friends to scheme and plot and figure out how to ensnare him. Forget that Bonnie is interested Stefan, too, HE’S ELENA’S AND SHE CAN’T HAVE HIM. (Oh wait, you say? Elena already has a really hot, popular, and kind boyfriend? Well yes, but she dumped him the moment something hotter came to town. Poor Matt. But really, he’s better off without her.) Anyway, so, Elena and friends start making up lies and spreading rumors and demanding favors from the lesser humans at the school who would do anything for the attention of the queen and her court. Oh yeah, she also begs Matt for favors… the guy she literally just dumped for Stefan… and now she’s asking Matt to help her win Stefan… (Matt has got to be the best character in this whole book, seriously.)<br /><br />Now I don’t want to get too spoilery, but the insta-love gets its chance to shine and proceeds somewhat like this:<br /><br /><i>“There’s an almost desperate hunger inside him when he kisses me, as if he wants to pull the soul out of my body…”</i><br /><br /><i>“She kissed the predatory mouth that had threatened her only a few moments ago.”</i><br /><br />Yeah that’s… healthy.<br /><br />So why didn’t I give this book one star? I’M A SUCKER FOR VAMPIRES, OKAY? I KINDA LIKED IT ANYWAY. But really because Damon. It was all for you, buddy.<br /><br />*P.S. My quotes are probably not punctuated correctly because I copied them down from the audiobook.<br /><br />*P.P.S I have no problem with a beautiful, popular, privileged character. It’s just that Elena is such an entitled brat and she doesn’t even grow. At least not in book 1.<br /><br />*P.P.P.S Have any of you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7100490.The_Forbidden_Game__The_Forbidden_Game___1_3_" title="The Forbidden Game (The Forbidden Game, #1-3) by L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forbidden Game</a> series also by L.J. Smith? Anyone notice how similar her heroines are? With the exception of Jenna being nicer than Elena, they could be the same person. Both perfect, beautiful blondes who are popular and make every man—including evil ones—fall desperately in love with them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14960832717362530224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10114390118472888089">As a fan of the show, I had heard hundreds of times that I shouldn't read these books. But I had money to spend and nothing to read so I did it. I shouldn't say I'm disappointed since I expected so little to begin with, but wow, I was still really let down. I knew it would be totally different, which I was okay with, but the book just isn't good. The amount of immaturity is ridiculous, and all those other reviews that say they declare their love in like a day and a half are not exaggerating. Tak</span>
  <span id="freeText10114390118472888089" style="display:none">As a fan of the show, I had heard hundreds of times that I shouldn't read these books. But I had money to spend and nothing to read so I did it. I shouldn't say I'm disappointed since I expected so little to begin with, but wow, I was still really let down. I knew it would be totally different, which I was okay with, but the book just isn't good. The amount of immaturity is ridiculous, and all those other reviews that say they declare their love in like a day and a half are not exaggerating. Take Caroline from the first half of season one, multiply her worst qualities by 10, and that's Elena in The Awakening. <br /><br />*Reread 1/8/18: My feelings haven't changed too much from 5 years ago, but this book isn't as bad as remembered. I think maybe I will bump it up to <b>2.5 stars</b> so it fall in the middle. I think the audiobook narrator did a good job making Elena as... well not likeable, but as <i>tolerable</i> as she can be.</span>

<div id="review_1497560430" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497560430" />
    <a title="DJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41664104-dj"><img alt="DJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578657426p2/41664104.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497560430?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DJ" href="/user/show/41664104-dj">DJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=north-america">north-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=series-to-continue-now">series-to-continue-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=young-adult-fantasy-dystopia-sci-fi">young-adult-fantasy-dystopia-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41664104-dj?shelf=published-1990s">published-1990s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497560430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9712552412625914592">A pretty enjoyable, though fairly standard, short and easy, teen-vampire-romance novel.<br/><br/>I was kind of disappointed with this book actually, and I honestly don't really know why I expected it to be more than what it was. I'd been excited for quite a while to start reading this series, and I'd hyped it up in my mind so much that I was sure it was going to be the best vampire book I'd read in ages, deep and dark and smart and full of twists & turns and non-stop action, adventure, excitement and plot</span>
  <span id="freeText9712552412625914592" style="display:none">A pretty enjoyable, though fairly standard, short and easy, teen-vampire-romance novel.<br /><br />I was kind of disappointed with this book actually, and I honestly don't really know why I expected it to be more than what it was. I'd been excited for quite a while to start reading this series, and I'd hyped it up in my mind so much that I was sure it was going to be the best vampire book I'd read in ages, deep and dark and smart and full of twists &amp; turns and non-stop action, adventure, excitement and plot. Not so much.<br /><br />But it was still an easy, enjoyable read and if I hadn't been convinced that I was in for an entirely different type of ride, then I'd probably have enjoyed it even more. <br /><br />I've heard it gets better after the first book so I shall persevere. Maybe my vampiric wishes will be granted :) I've also heard it's way better than the TV show but I can't comment on that as I've never actually seen it - I just can't bring myself to look past the fact that the male leads are <i>clearly</i> about 35, and everybody's acting as if they reasonably pass for 16 year old high school students.<br /><br />One more thing - every description I've seen of this book bizarrely describes the plot as 'a love triangle between a high school girl and two vampire brothers'. I can't comment on the rest of the series, but that is not remotely what this book is about at all. It's better than that. <br /><br />Here's how <i>I'd</i> describe the plot:<br /><br /><i>Beautiful Elena Gilbert returns from spending her summer in Paris to start her senior year of high school. Upon arriving at school, she sees a new student has started - the gorgeous, mysterious Stefan who Elena is immediately drawn to... and who is the first guy ever to brush her off. Now she is more determined than ever to make him hers.<br />Stefan is a centuries old vampire trying to make a new life for himself in Mystic Falls. When he sees Elena, he is instantly reminded of Katherine, his first love, and Damon, his brother he has not spoken to in centuries... because of what happened to Katherine.<br />When people in Mystic Falls start being attacked around the same time that Stefan arrives, even Stefan begins to question his own innocence.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9712552412625914592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_544824746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/544824746" />
    <a title="Aiman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16076980-aiman"><img alt="Aiman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405936664p2/16076980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/544824746?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aiman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aiman" href="/user/show/16076980-aiman">Aiman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=awful">awful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16076980-aiman?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer544824746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1517776259959030762">I only read about 1-2 chapters of this book. And I after searching high and low, reading through thesauruses and pondering for hours, I have come up with the <i>perfect</i> word to describe The Awakening (The Vampire Diaries #1) <b>Eww.</b> I can hear you applauding me so I shall take a virtual bow. Thank you. Thank you. I know, right? Eww, eww, eww.<br/><br/>What do we have here? A vain, self-absorbed and depressed teenager and an ancient, lovesick vampire who devours...wait for it... fluffy, innocent, fluffy, cute, f</span>
  <span id="freeText1517776259959030762" style="display:none">I only read about 1-2 chapters of this book. And I after searching high and low, reading through thesauruses and pondering for hours, I have come up with the <i>perfect</i> word to describe The Awakening (The Vampire Diaries #1) <b>Eww.</b> I can hear you applauding me so I shall take a virtual bow. Thank you. Thank you. I know, right? Eww, eww, eww.<br /><br />What do we have here? A vain, self-absorbed and depressed teenager and an ancient, lovesick vampire who devours...wait for it... fluffy, innocent, fluffy, cute, fluffy rabbits. How utterly unforgivable. <s>Humanity</s> Vampire-ity has reached a whole new level of cruelty. Someone call the RSPCA. I reached the part where Elena the egomaniac is 'insulted' after being ignored by Stefan the sadistic rabbit eater. And then I tried to throw down the book with a disgusted sigh. Unfortunately, I was reading a PDF file of the book on my laptop and was irritated- as you can imagine- that I couldn't fulfill my intention. Alas, I had to contend myself with closing the file with a vehement click of the mouse and cussing a stream of unladylike words. <b>
  <u> IMPORTANT NOTE:</u>
</b> There is no joy like the joy of reading the physical, hard copy of a book. It can be kissed, hugged, cried on, stained and of course, shredded into pieces too :D And because I believe that the last one is sacrilege, I think it should be replaced by the guilty book being thrown from a height of approximately 1.5 meters (not anymore, lest the book should get seriously harmed- which is also sacrilege) and being told in a strict voice "Bad book! BAD BOOK!"<br /><br />Anyway, after all of this, it was clear that the book was going to be a hideous mixture of lame romance and disturbing dramas of high school. So I swore at the book again and went to read something else.<br /><br />Yay! <br />The End.<br /><br />P.S. The TV series is <i>much</i> better than the books.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E6urzjU8HHonI79P4iHSt4i5SSPlI+g6MQihf/tteYoeyWx6CKjAk7s9toEd40ABL7OpWTz1FbzwiBxSRCNrpA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9+hDXqxi74a+qWRw9Yoiw1D9FGnk/3uubMsQhYSoulT6ioTqkfYzbyK3bb4KSLB19/f0Ez0phiitS62oO+aoeg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8226244610371586727">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series'>https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br/><br/><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in th</span>
  <span id="freeText8226244610371586727" style="display:none">I have a new blog about my Vampire Diaries fanfic.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5539821-l-j-smith-s-new-vampires-diaries-series">https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog...</a><br /><br /><b>L.J. SMITH</b>, Lisa Jane Smith, is the New York Times #1 Bestselling author of <i>The Vampire Diaries, The Secret Circle, The Forbidden Game, Dark Visions, Wildworld</i> and <i>Night World</i> series. She has written over two dozen books for children and young adults, and has enjoyed writing every one of them. She lives in the Bay Area of California, with a backyard that is full of flowers, which she adores, especially with many different shades of roses.<br /><br />She loves to visit a friend's little cabin in the Point Reyes National Seashore area, which has lots of trees, lots of animals, lots of beaches to walk on, and lots of places to hike. Once, while hiking, she saw a snow-white buck which allowed her to follow it nearly half a mile. She also likes to collect things: angels (they remind her of her late mother), tiny boxes from different countries or of fanciful shape, nineteenth century children's literature, and books about quantum physics--especially about the mystery of the dark energy in the universe. A militant optimist, she is also part of the Velociraptor Sisterhood (a fancy way of saying that she likes to read, write and discuss books with strong female characters), and she has traveled extensively in Europe and the Far East. The two countries she loves to visit most are Great Britain, with its historic monuments and amazing country landscapes, and Japan, with its bustling urban life and exquisite mountain scenery.<br /><br />Her favorite current writer is Terry Pratchett, the author of the Discworld series, for its wild and witty satires on life, death, war, love, assassins, coppers, and Australia. Her favorite classical writer is Jane Austen. Her favorite poets are Robert Frost and Emily Dickinson. Her favorite movies are The Seven Samurai and Avatar (analyze that!). She doesn't have a favorite TV show, because she doesn't have time to watch TV (and only owns one for playing movies).<br /><br />Her favorite people are her readers, each of whom she cherishes with deep and lasting affection.<br /><br /><i>Note: L. J. Smith wrote books 1-7 of The Vampire Diaries series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. wrote books 1-3 of The Secret Circle series. After that, a ghostwriter took over the rest of the series. L. J. did not write any of the Originals or Stefan's Diaries. These were written by Kevin Williamson and/or various ghostwritters.</i> <br /></span>
